## 2026-06-21

- **Fix (web chat streaming cursor/statuses after tool-loop replies):** Restored the inline streaming cursor/status row under live assistant text after the first streamed reply. The live tool/project/retrieval status was still being attached to the assistant bubble, but `ChatMessageBubble` hid `InlineStreamingStatus` as soon as `message.content` became non-empty. The fix tracks live text deltas separately: while text is actively streaming, the next line shows an empty pulsing cursor; when streaming pauses on a tool/project/retrieval/compaction boundary, the same row shows cursor + current status text (for example “Собираю контекст”, “смотрю страницу”). Separate activity banners are not reintroduced. Added localized ru/en lifecycle statuses for browser, document, grep, glob, shell, exec, quota_status, memory_write, skill, background_task, and normalized knowledge/files tool labels so new ADR-123 workspace tools do not fall back to generic “Working on it”. Gate: `chat-message.test.tsx`, `activity-badge.test.tsx`, `use-chat.test.tsx`, web lint, web typecheck, format:check PASS.

- **Fix (ADR-123 prompt policy alignment: media/document routing + workspace tool loop):** Tightened model-facing tool instructions without broadening the prompt. The global media policy no longer advertises carousel/series as a general route; `image_edit` is scoped to visual edits of existing images, while uploaded images/files used as source material for PDFs, Word/DOCX, Excel/XLSX, decks, reports, OCR, tables, or other documents route to `document` (or inline vision when no deliverable is needed). The workspace category now expresses the intended ADR-123 loop: discover files with `glob`, search contents with `grep`, use `files` for file IO, and use `shell` proactively for execution/verification rather than search shortcuts. Updated the ADR-119 golden prompt snapshot and bootstrap prompt regression test. Gate: focused bootstrap + golden snapshot tests, format:check, API lint, API typecheck PASS.

- **Fix (ADR-124 DeepSeek live correctness: thinking-mode tool loops + text-only multimodal):** Two live `persai-dev` DeepSeek failures fixed without legacy shims. **(1) Tool-loop `reasoning_content` round-trip.** DeepSeek V4 runs in thinking mode by default and rejects any subsequent tool-loop request that does not echo back the `reasoning_content` it produced alongside `tool_calls` (`400 "The reasoning_content in the thinking mode must be passed back to the API."`) — which broke every DeepSeek turn that called a tool. The provider-gateway DeepSeek adapter now captures `reasoning_content` from both the non-stream (`message.reasoning_content`) and stream (`delta.reasoning_content`) responses, surfaces it on `ProviderGatewayTextGenerateResult.reasoningContent`, and echoes it back on the assistant tool-call message in `buildMessages`; the runtime threads it onto each `ProviderGatewayToolExchange.reasoningContent` at the tool-history push sites (stream + sync paths). DeepSeek tool calls are now forced sequential (`parallel_tool_calls: false`) so each assistant turn carries exactly one tool call and the reasoning echo stays canonical (matching DeepSeek's official function-calling example). OpenAI/Anthropic ignore the new field, so their paths are unchanged. **(2) Text-only multimodal handling.** DeepSeek's `/chat/completions` API is text-only and 400s on inline image/PDF blocks, which silently broke turns with attachments. A new `runtime-text-only-multimodal-sanitizer` converts every non-text content block to text for text-only main providers: inline image/PDF blocks (current-turn uploads in the base messages, hydrated once before the tool loop; and `files.preview` follow-up blocks) are described once via the plan's `systemTool` slot model (a vision-capable OpenAI/Anthropic model) and replaced with that text. Vision-capable main providers keep their raw blocks untouched. If no vision-capable helper is available or the describe fails, the block becomes an explicit placeholder (`"[Image … could not be analyzed for this model.]"`) — never raw pixels and never a silent drop. Already-text content (txt/csv/html/doc converted upstream) passes straight through. The admin plan validator now also requires the `systemTool` slot to resolve to a vision-capable provider (OpenAI/Anthropic), since that slot doubles as the vision describe helper. Local gate green (repo lint, format:check, api/web/runtime/provider-gateway typecheck, DeepSeek adapter + admin-plan + sanitizer unit tests); DeepSeek live re-validation in `persai-dev` pending the next deploy.

- **Fix (ADR-121 project routing + tool-loop readability; CI green after ADR-124 test drift):** Project chat mode no longer bypasses ordinary routing or pins every project turn to the reasoning slot. The project execution contract still enables pull-first file/knowledge workflow and project activity events, but `turn-routing.service` now lets project turns flow through the same precheck/classifier path as other modes; simple project turns remain normal/premium depending on the existing deep-mode nudge, and reasoning is used only for genuinely deep signals such as PDF/code-heavy/depth-cue work. Also fixed streamed tool-loop readability: assistant text segments emitted before successive tool calls are separated by a blank line instead of being flattened into one inline sentence, while prefix/dedupe handling still preserves cumulative provider deltas. While repeating CI checks, fixed two ADR-124 test drifts that were already failing `main`: session-compaction request/lease counters now account for the added prompt-cache-retention smoke, and provider-gateway warmup tests now account for DeepSeek managed-provider secret resolution.

- **ADR-124 implemented locally (provider-agnostic model routing, prompt-cache retention capability, provider-error fallback, DeepSeek adapter):** Runtime model slots now carry provider+model truth independently from the account default, so normal/premium/reasoning/system/retrieval slots can resolve any active chat model from any catalog provider while keeping the existing single global fallback target. `promptCacheRetention` is now a catalog/model-profile capability (`in_memory`/`24h`/`null`) and OpenAI prompt-cache request shaping reads it from the resolved slot instead of a hardcoded constant, fixing `gpt-5.5`'s extended-retention requirement. Anthropic structured-output schema sanitation now strips unsupported constraint keywords such as numeric min/max before provider dispatch. Provider text errors now carry semantic kinds (`billing_quota`, `rate_limit`, `capacity`, `provider_auth`, `invalid_request`, etc.) through provider-gateway/runtime boundaries; fallback is allowed pre-first-token for provider-side satisfiable failures, while malformed requests remain non-fallback. DeepSeek is registered as a credential-gated managed text provider using the existing PersAI provider-key secret store (`deepseek/api-key`) and a thin OpenAI-compatible Chat Completions adapter at `https://api.deepseek.com`; active catalog defaults add `deepseek-v4-flash` and `deepseek-v4-pro` with 1M context / 384k max output and token-metered pricing. Contracts/admin UI were updated for per-slot provider+model selection and DeepSeek runtime keys. Local gate green; DeepSeek live validation remains pending until credentials are configured and the deploy is live.

- **Change (ADR-123 exec image): curated doc/data/image baseline preinstalled in sandbox-exec.** Expanded the immutable exec image instead of relying on runtime `apt-get` (blocked by read-only root FS) or ad-hoc `pip install` for common work. System packages now include `libzbar0`, `tesseract-ocr` (+ eng/rus), `poppler-utils`, `ghostscript`, `git`, `unzip`, `zip`, headless GL/X helpers, image codecs, and XML libs. Python venv now also ships `xlsxwriter`, `pypdf`, `reportlab`, `pyzbar`, `qrcode`, `pytesseract`, `beautifulsoup4`, `lxml`, `jinja2`, `seaborn`, `python-dateutil`, `pyyaml`, `requests` alongside the existing pandas/openpyxl/python-docx/weasyprint/pdfplumber stack. Build self-checks import the expanded Python baseline and verify `tesseract`, `pdftotext`, `gs`, and `git`. Runtime `pip install` remains only for rare extras into `/workspace/.local`.

- **Fix (ADR-123 documents mode B): queued XLSX/DOCX jobs now replay as `create_data_document` instead of being downgraded to the PDF renderer.** Live audit before push: XLSX job `dca8f91f-...` and DOCX job `9d2a92de-...` failed `document_artifacts_missing`; nested provider status was `invalid_path` / `render_html_to_pdf outputFileName must end with .pdf`, proving they hit the HTML→PDF renderer. Root cause: `AssistantDocumentJobSchedulerService.parseRequestPayload()` did not accept `create_data_document` and only preserved `pdf|pptx`, so stored queued requests with `descriptorMode: "create_data_document"` + `outputFormat: "xlsx"|"docx"` replayed as `create_pdf_document` and routed incorrectly. Fixed parser to preserve `create_data_document`, `xlsx`, and `docx`; widened completion/failure framing unions; added regression test. Note: two latest PDF jobs delivered; the one fresh PDF failure was model HTML-generation quality (`body text length=59 < 120` after 3 attempts), not sandbox/push.

- **Change (ADR-123 sandbox follow-up): session pod idle TTL shortened to 15 min, and runtime `pip install` now writes to `/workspace/.local` instead of read-only `/opt/venv`.** With `sandbox-pool` `min-nodes=1` + `sandbox-exec-prepull`, long pod TTL is no longer needed to hide cold starts; `SANDBOX_EXEC_SESSION_IDLE_TTL_MS` is now `900000` (15 min) in config + dev Helm values, while the reaper interval stays 2 min. The exec image keeps read-only root FS and immutable preinstalled `/opt/venv`, but runtime package installs are now user-site installs: venv created with `--system-site-packages`, `PYTHONUSERBASE=/workspace/.local`, `PIP_USER=1`, and `/workspace/.local/bin` first on PATH (including login shells). So ordinary shell commands like `pip install colorama==0.4.6` write to the session-scoped writable workspace, not system site-packages. Build self-checks assert user-site visibility. Tests/config fixtures updated.

- **Fix (ADR-123 sandbox workspace push): large workspace tar must be streamed to Kubernetes exec stdin in bounded chunks, not as one giant WebSocket frame.** Correct root cause for the new post-deploy error `process_spawn_failed` / `"Workspace push verification failed: tar extraction marker missing"`. Live DB truth for assistant `c2df1500-ec77-4224-891d-efc32a16c810`: the assistant workspace is **165 files / 52,220,007 bytes** (not 97,933 files — that was an operator/debugger quoting mistake that inspected the sandbox control-plane container's `/workspace` app repo). Reproduced with the real hydrated workspace against the live session pod: local tar succeeded (`52,582,400` bytes), but `Readable.from([tarball])` delivered **0 bytes** into the pod; remote `tar` then printed `tar: This does not look like a tar archive`, so no marker was written. The exact same tar streamed in **64 KiB chunks** delivered `52,582,400` bytes byte-for-byte (`sha256` match) and `tar -tf` passed. Root fix: `execWorkspaceTarPush` now feeds stdin through `readBufferInChunks(tarball, 64 * 1024)` instead of a single-buffer Readable. The existing marker + stdin-less verify stays authoritative; no readiness sleep and no blind retry loop. Added regression test that large push payloads are split into WebSocket-safe chunks and reassemble byte-for-byte. Gate: sandbox typecheck · sandbox tests 28/28 PASS.

- **Change (ADR-123 founder directive): the reusable exec pod is now keyed per `(assistantId, workspaceId)` instead of per chat session, + the `sandbox-pool` warm node is enabled (min-nodes 0 → 1, 1-month trial).** **(1) Per-workspace pod.** Previously each chat (`runtimeSessionId`) got its own exec pod, so a second chat for the same assistant cold-started a fresh pod even though one was already warm. Now all chats of one assistant workspace share a single pod named `ses-<sha256(assistantId:workspaceId)>`. Safe because the pod's `/workspace` is re-pushed from the control plane on every job (pod identity is purely a warmth optimization, never file truth) and the existing `assistantId+workspaceId` Postgres workspace lease already serializes every job for that workspace — so the shared pod is never used concurrently, even across chats. The pod now carries `persai.io/assistant-id` + `persai.io/workspace-id` annotations (replacing `persai.io/session-id`); the idle-TTL reaper derives last-activity via `sandboxJob.findFirst({ where: { assistantId, workspaceId } })`. Old per-session pods drain naturally — without the new annotations the reaper falls back to pod-creation age and evicts them after the idle TTL. The control-plane GCS workspace snapshot (keyed by `assistantId+runtimeSessionId`) is unchanged and orthogonal. Sessionless jobs (`runtimeSessionId === null`) stay ephemeral. Files: `apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts` (`runInPod`/`runInSessionPod`/`ensureSessionPodRunning`/`buildSessionPodName` thread `assistantId`+`workspaceId`; annotations + reaper query re-keyed), `apps/sandbox/src/sandbox.service.ts` (the three exec wrappers + dispatcher pass `request.assistantId`/`request.workspaceId`). Tests updated for the new keying + annotations; sandbox 27/27. **(2) Warm node enabled live.** `gcloud container node-pools update sandbox-pool --zone europe-west1-b --enable-autoscaling --min-nodes 1 --max-nodes 2` applied (dev cluster is **zonal** `europe-west1-b` — RUNBOOK §8 corrected from the wrong `--region europe-west1`, max left at the cluster's actual 2). One sandbox node now stays Ready and the `sandbox-exec-prepull` DaemonSet (`sandboxExec.prepull.enabled: true`) keeps the exec image cached on it, so the first command after idle starts in ~2–5s instead of ~100s. Founder reviews the standing-node cost after ~1 month. Gate: sandbox typecheck · 27/27 tests PASS. **Effective after the next `sandbox` control-plane redeploy; the warm node is already live.**

- **Fix (ADR-123 — THE sandbox "shell doesn't work" root cause): workspace push success was read off the same exec socket that streams the tar on stdin, and `@kubernetes/client-node` drops that channel under a payload.** Every `shell`/`exec`/`render_html_to_pdf` job was failing `process_spawn_failed` / `"Workspace push closed without success (stderr: none)"`, intermittently, and it persisted after the cold-start deploy. **Live diagnosis (not assumed):** queried `sandbox_jobs` on `persai-dev` — every recent failure had `exec_pod_name: null` + that exact message, and one waited **80s** (the pod was up) and still failed → not a cold-start timeout. Reproduced with the real `@kubernetes/client-node` from inside the control-plane pod against the live session pod: a **1 KB** stdin payload returns the success sentinel, but **200 KB / 2 MB** payloads return `status=Success` (the remote `tar` exits 0) while the exec **stdout channel is silently dropped** (sentinel lost) and the status frame races the socket close. Root: the 2026-06-20 "reliable workspace push" rework (commits `9eaf30f8`/`96d3c288`) made success detection depend on a sentinel printed on that same stdin-laden socket, so every real (>~1 KB) workspace push reported failure even though extraction succeeded — a regression vs. the prior streaming push. **Root fix (`apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`):** decouple data transfer from success detection. The push exec streams the tar and writes a marker file **only when `tar` exits 0** (`rm -f marker; tar … && printf ok > marker`); its own stdout/status are intentionally ignored (it resolves on a clean close, rejects only on a real connection failure). A **separate stdin-less verify exec** then checks the marker — with no stdin multiplexed, its stdout + status frame are reliable (proven 4/4 with 2 MB payloads in-cluster). Missing marker ⇒ retryable `process_spawn_failed`; the command and pull never run on a failed push. This supersedes the sentinel-on-push-stdout scheme from the 2026-06-20 entry. Tests: new regression test asserting success comes from the stdin-less verify (verify reports marker-missing → push fails, command never runs); the shared exec mock now defaults unseeded calls to success so tests are resilient to the extra round-trip; sandbox 27/27. Gate: sandbox typecheck · lint · prettier PASS. **Effective after the next `sandbox` control-plane redeploy.**

- **Fix (ADR-123 documents pre-deploy): failed document jobs (`document_artifacts_missing`) now retry transient sandbox infra flakes; retired `document_render:pdfmonkey` price removed.** A live test PDF failed after 24s with `document_artifacts_missing` ("worker completed without deliverable artifacts"). Root cause (from the job's `providerStatusJson`): the render's sandbox job hit a workspace-push flake — `errorCode: "process_spawn_failed"`, `"Workspace push closed without success (stderr: none)"`, `retryable: false` — so the job died after **1/5** attempts instead of retrying. The chain: `apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts` `createBridgeError` defaulted `blocked=true`; the push-failure path (and all pod read/create/status/terminal/provisioning + local-tar push failures) created the error with that default; `sandbox.service.normalizeSandboxError` maps `blocked → status "blocked"` (a policy block) instead of `"failed"`; and the document worker's `renderHtmlToPdf` derives `retryable = (result.status === "failed")` — so a `blocked` status is non-retryable and the scheduler reports the misleading `document_artifacts_missing`. **Root fix:** bridge errors are now **operational/retryable by default** (`createBridgeError` default `blocked=false`); only genuine non-retryable blocks pass `blocked=true` explicitly — the stdout/stderr resource-limit collector and the command-runtime-budget `process_timeout` (where retrying the same command would time out again). Spawn / pod-provisioning / push failures now surface as `failed` → the async document render job retries (and, with the cold-start provisioning budget + warm pool, lands on a warm pod). This aligns `process_spawn_failed` and the provisioning `process_timeout` with the already-correct `sandbox_failed` (exec/pull) handling, which already passed `blocked:false`. No runtime-adapter change needed — the existing `status === "failed"` test now evaluates correctly. Interactive `shell`/`exec` are unaffected (a spawn failure surfaces as action `"skipped"` rather than `"blocked"`, same `reason` code, still `isError`). **Also (Slice 5 follow-up):** Slice 5 removed PDFMonkey from code (`document_render` provider defaults are gamma-only) but the tool-path pricing **catalog merge preserves stored rows**, so the stale `document_render:pdfmonkey` row (price 8000) kept showing in Admin > Tools. Idempotent data migration `apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260621130000_adr123_drop_retired_pdfmonkey_render_price` strips it from the stored `tool_path_pricing_catalog`; the prod `persai-dev` row was also removed live (`rows 8 → 7`, only `document_render:gamma` remains). Files: `apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`, new migration. Gate: sandbox typecheck · lint · format:check PASS. **Effective after the next sandbox redeploy + migration; the pdfmonkey card is already gone in `persai-dev`.**

- **Fix (ADR-123 Slice 3 cold-start): the first sandbox command after idle no longer fails; warm pool re-opened.** Live diagnosis: the first `shell`/`exec` after idle took ~104s (sandbox node autoscale + multi-GB exec-image pull) and _failed_ because four budgets were sized for the warm path and conflated pod startup with command runtime — (1) `waitForPodRunning` used `policy.maxProcessRuntimeMs` (15s) as the pod-ready deadline → `process_timeout`; (2) the control-plane running-job watchdog (`maxProcessRuntimeMs + grace`, ~30s) → `sandbox_execution_timeout`; (3) the runtime `resolveCompletionTimeoutMs` (~40s) abandoned the job; (4) queued-stale 45s. The ADR-123 Slice 3 "warm pool DEFERRED (cold start ~2–4s)" premise was empirically wrong. **Two-track fix.** Reliability: new dedicated pod-provisioning budget `SANDBOX_EXEC_POD_PROVISION_BUDGET_MS` (control plane) + `RUNTIME_SANDBOX_POD_PROVISION_BUDGET_MS` (runtime), default 240s, threaded through `waitForPodRunning`, the running-job watchdog (`maxRunningMs` now adds the provision budget), and the runtime completion timeout; `maxProcessRuntimeMs` is now used _only_ as the per-command cap — a cold start succeeds (waits once) instead of failing. Latency (warm pool re-opened): a `sandbox-exec-prepull` DaemonSet keeps the exec image cached on every sandbox node (Helm, `sandboxExec.prepull.enabled`), paired with a ≥1-min-node `sandbox-pool` (operational `gcloud node-pools update`, documented in `infra/dev/gke/RUNBOOK.md` §Slice 3.8) — first command after idle drops from ~100s to seconds. The prepull pod only sleeps, holds no secrets, never runs model code. Files: `packages/config/src/{sandbox,runtime}-config.ts`, `apps/sandbox/src/{exec-pod-bridge,sandbox}.service.ts`, `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/sandbox-client.service.ts`, `infra/helm/templates/sandbox-exec-prepull-daemonset.yaml`, `infra/helm/values-dev.yaml`. Tests: bridge + sandbox config literals updated; new runtime assertion that the completion budget ≥ the provision budget; 9 runtime config literals updated. Note: the assistant-reported "Workspace push WebSocket closed without status" was stale — that string is not in the deployed code; control-plane logs show exec jobs succeeding on a warm pod. Gate: helm lint + template (prepull renders with the correct exec image) · sandbox typecheck · runtime typecheck · bridge + sandbox-client tests PASS. **Effective after the next runtime + sandbox redeploy; warm node requires the one-time `gcloud` step.**

- **Fix (ADR-123 Slice 7): `grep`/`glob` now surface in `/admin/presets`, `/admin/plans`, AND to the model (two missing wirings).** Slice 7 shipped the catalog rows + runtime projection but missed two control-plane wirings, so the tools were invisible everywhere despite existing & `status:active` in the DB:
  - **(1) `/admin/presets` order gate.** Slice 7 added `grep`/`glob` to the **web** `PROMPT_CONSTRUCTOR_MODEL_TOOL_ORDER` but not the **API** copy in `apps/api/.../prompt-constructor-tool-metadata.ts`. That API list is the real gate — `ManageAdminToolPromptMetadataService.list()` iterates the API order and pulls matching catalog rows, so any code absent from it is filtered server-side (and `isPromptConstructorModelToolCode` rejects metadata edits). Added `grep`/`glob` after `files` in the API order (mirroring web).
  - **(2) Plan tool activations never backfilled.** Verified against the live DB: `files`/`shell` had `PlanCatalogToolActivation` rows on every plan but `grep`/`glob` had **zero** on any plan — so they were absent from the plan editor and there was nothing to materialize for the model (a reapply did nothing). Root cause: `SeedToolCatalogService.syncToolActivations` only runs when a plan has zero activations (to avoid reverting operator edits), and `syncNonPlanManagedToolPolicyAcrossPlans` deliberately skips plan-managed tools — so a NEW plan-managed tool never receives a row on already-configured plans. Added `backfillMissingPlanManagedToolActivations()` (runs on API boot): **create-if-absent** rows for plan-managed tools across all plans using `STARTER_TRIAL_TOOL_POLICY` defaults (grep/glob → `active`, dailyCallLimit 20), **never** updating existing rows (operator edits preserved); platform-managed tools skipped. New plan-managed tools still need a reapply/rollout to reach already-published assistants (same as any admin tool toggle). The missing prod rows for `grep`/`glob` were also created directly on `persai-dev` (12 rows = grep+glob × 6 plans) for immediate effect ahead of the redeploy. Tests: `seed-tool-catalog.test.ts` gains a backfill case (planA gets only the missing grep row, planB gets files+grep, skill skipped, defaults active/20). Verified: api typecheck PASS, `seed-tool-catalog.test.ts` PASS, `manage-admin-tool-prompt-metadata.service.test.ts` PASS. **`/admin/presets` display needs the api+web redeploy; `/admin/plans` + model visibility are live now (after a reapply) thanks to the direct row insert.**

- **ADR-123 post-program config tuning (founder directive — open delivery MIME + broaden egress; both within D3's deny-all+allowlist model):** Two operator-facing openings so the sandbox stops hitting walls, with the security boundary unchanged. **(1) Delivery MIME allowlist → allow-all.** `DEFAULT_RUNTIME_SANDBOX_POLICY.artifactMimeAllowlist` is now `["*/*"]` (was a 12-entry curated list); `RuntimeFilesToolService.assertMimeAllowed` treats `*/*` (and `*`) as the allow-all sentinel (empty list already meant allow-all; any other non-empty list stays exact-match). A **data migration** (`apps/api/prisma/migrations/20260621120000_adr123_open_delivery_mime_allowlist`, data-only — no schema change) rewrites every plan's stored `billing_provider_hints.sandboxPolicy.artifactMimeAllowlist` to `["*/*"]` (jsonb_set, `create_missing=false`, skips rows already `["*/*"]`) so all plans are uniformly open in the DB and the founder never edits it per-plan; plans with no stored override inherit the new default. **This does not widen the safety boundary** — the true ceiling is the persist-time media validation (`apps/api/.../media/media-security-policy.ts`: `ALLOWED_MEDIA_MIMES` + `DANGEROUS_FILE_EXTENSIONS`, which blocks `.exe/.js/.sh/.svg/...`), which runs on every produced artifact regardless of the delivery allowlist. The per-plan "Allowed delivery mime types" admin field still works for narrowing if ever wanted. **(2) Egress allowlist broadened (still Claude-style deny-all + allowlist, NOT open internet).** `egressProxy.allowedDomains` (`infra/helm/values-dev.yaml`) adds `.github.com` + `.githubusercontent.com` (git clone / VCS `pip install` / release + raw fetches) alongside the existing PyPI + npm entries; deny-all default and D3 secret-exfiltration protection preserved (open/unfiltered egress was explicitly rejected). **Tests:** runtime files-tool wildcard allow-all assertion (image/png no longer blocked under `["*/*"]`, exact-match block path unchanged). Gate: lint · format:check · 5 typechecks · affected tests. **Deploy residual:** the data migration pauses on the `persai-dev-migrations` environment per CI policy; the egress allowlist change applies on ArgoCD sync (Squid ConfigMap reload).

- **ADR-123 Slice 7 landed (inline `grep`/`glob` workspace tools + autonomous `shell` + `<tool_usage_policy>` workspace category):** Final ADR-123 implementation slice. **New inline tools** `grep` (content search) and `glob` (filename discovery) execute on the sandbox **control plane** as TRUSTED PersAI-owned subprocesses invoking the preinstalled `rg` (ripgrep) / `fd` binaries against the hydrated `workspaceRoot` — the SAME workspace source the existing `files` read handler uses. They are NEVER routed through `ExecPodBridgeService.runInPod` (no exec pod), so D2's control-plane secret-free/trusted invariant holds (trusted binary + model **data** args, not model-authored commands). **Arg safety:** model-supplied values (pattern, glob/type, path) are passed as an argv ARRAY with a leading `--` terminator (never a shell string; `shell: false`), and the optional `path` is normalized through `resolveWorkspacePath` so it cannot escape `workspaceRoot` (escaping paths fail the job before any binary spawns). Each run has a hard timeout (`policy.maxProcessRuntimeMs`), a stdout byte cap (`policy.maxStdoutBytes`), and a match/path count cap (grep 200 matches, glob 500 paths) with a `truncated` flag. **Contract** (`packages/runtime-contract`): new `RuntimeGrepMatch` / `RuntimeGrepToolResult` (`matches[{file,line,text}]`, `matchCount`, `truncated`) and `RuntimeGlobToolResult` (sorted relative `paths`, `truncated`), both `executionMode: "inline"`. **Sandbox** (`apps/sandbox/src/sandbox.service.ts`): `executeTool` gains `case "grep"`/`case "glob"` → `executeGrepAction`/`executeGlobAction` → `runTrustedControlPlaneBinary` (argv-array `spawn`, cwd=workspaceRoot); `rg` exit 1 (no matches) treated as success, 2+ as error; results serialized into the existing `resultPayload.content` JSON. **Dockerfile** (`apps/sandbox/Dockerfile`): control-plane image now installs `ripgrep` + `fd-find` and symlinks `fdfind`→`fd` (mirrors the exec-image apt install). **Projection** (`native-tool-projection.ts`): `createGrepToolDefinition` / `createGlobToolDefinition` (grep schema = `pattern` required + `path`/`glob`/`type`/`caseInsensitive`/`contextLines`; glob = `pattern` required + `path`) projected after the files block when policy is enabled+inline. **Policy/Catalog** (`runtime-tool-policy.ts`, `tool-catalog-data.ts`): grep/glob added to `TOOL_EXECUTION_MODE_BY_CODE` (`inline`) and `hasNativeModelExecution` (require `sandboxEnabled`); `files` usage guidance now routes content search → grep, filename find → glob; new grep/glob catalog rows (`capabilityGroup: workspace_ops`); the `shell` `modelUsageGuidance` was REWRITTEN to encourage proactive multi-step autonomous use (pipelines, builds, scripts) and route search to grep/glob (removed the old "reserve shell"/"prefer files" discouragement and the `grep -r 'TODO'` shell-search example); `grep`/`glob` set `active:true` in `STARTER_TRIAL_TOOL_POLICY` (matching `files`; exec/shell stay inactive). **Routing** (`turn-execution.service.ts` + new `runtime-grep-glob-tool.service.ts`): grep/glob tool calls dispatch through a thin inline service that posts a sandbox job (toolCode `grep`/`glob`) via the `files`-style control-plane path and parses the structured result; per-turn caps added (`tool-budget-policy.ts`: grep 10, glob 10). **Prompt** (`bootstrap-preset-data.ts`): additive `<category name="workspace">` inside `<tool_usage_policy>` `<category_rules>` (content search→grep, filename find→glob, read/edit→files, multi-step exec→shell, new document→document); `<priority_order>` and the `<tool_usage_policy>` wrapper unchanged (ADR-119 structural golden tests stay green; the byte-snapshot fixture `adr119-golden-prompt-snapshot.expected.txt` regenerated — diff is exactly the +7-line workspace category). **Web admin** (`apps/web/app/admin/presets/page.tsx`): `grep`/`glob` added to `PROMPT_CONSTRUCTOR_MODEL_TOOL_ORDER` (right after `files`, before `exec`/`shell`) so the catalog rows are visible/manageable in `/admin/presets`; `capabilityGroup` `workspace_ops` already in the `ToolPromptState` union (no new group). **Tests:** sandbox grep/glob (argv safety + `--` terminator, workspace-escape rejection without spawning, match-count cap + truncation, fd sorted relative paths) 26/26; api policy (grep/glob inline + enabled) + bootstrap workspace-category presence; runtime projection (grep/glob projected, shell discouragement gone) + turn-execution dispatch (grep/glob → inline service, tool-order lists updated); web presets 6/6. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api`/`@persai/web`/`@persai/runtime`/`@persai/provider-gateway`/`@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · sandbox/api/runtime/web test suites PASS. **Deploy residual:** the control-plane `sandbox` image must be rebuilt so `rg`/`fd` are present on PATH (inline grep/glob fail without them).

- **ADR-123 Slice 6 landed (documents mode B — model-writes-code Excel/DOCX/data-PDF in the sandbox; create-only):** New parallel document path alongside mode A (HTML→WeasyPrint). New model-facing `descriptorMode: "create_data_document"` plus `outputFormat` values `xlsx`/`docx` (alongside `pdf`/`pptx`); routing forces `documentType: "data_document"`, `provider: "sandbox"`, defaulting `outputFormat` to `xlsx` when omitted. **Prisma** (additive migration `20260621000001_adr123_slice6_data_document`): `AssistantDocumentType += data_document`, `AssistantDocumentDescriptorMode += create_data_document`, `AssistantDocumentOutputFormat += xlsx, docx` (each `ALTER TYPE ... ADD VALUE` in its own statement). **Contract** (`packages/runtime-contract`): the document `outputFormat`/`documentType`/`descriptorMode` unions widened across tool-result, job-run, completion, and read shapes; `DEFAULT_RUNTIME_SANDBOX_POLICY.artifactMimeAllowlist += ` the Office xlsx/docx MIME types; new `document_code_generation` provider request classification. **Worker** (`runtime-document-provider-adapter.service.ts`): early mode-B branch → `runCodeDocumentPath` authors a single self-contained Python 3 program (preinstalled `openpyxl`/`python-docx`/`pandas`/`matplotlib`/`weasyprint` stack; no network, no `pip install`), runs it in the sandbox via the new `execute_document_code` toolCode, performs **one bounded self-repair retry** (stderr fed back into a second authoring call; terminal `document_code_failed` after the second failure — never a loop), validates the artifact (xlsx/docx = `PK\x03\x04` ZIP magic + min size; pdf = existing `%PDF-` validator), persists the GCS-downloaded file as `runtime_output`, and soft-deletes the transient `sandbox_output`. **Two-tier source ingestion (founder-approved supersession of inline source text):** TIER 1 mounts raw source files via `RuntimeSandboxJobRequest.mountedFileRefs` into `/workspace/sources/<name>` and the code-gen prompt instructs the model to read them natively (pdfplumber/python-docx/openpyxl/pandas) — source size is no longer bounded by the output-token budget and text is never inlined; TIER 2 runs a runtime-layer `pdf-parse` text-layer probe (`buildDataDocumentSourcePlan` + `probePdfTextLayer`, threshold 32 alnum chars) and, for scanned PDFs / images, runs the existing `document-extraction.service` OCR and mounts a `<name>.ocr.txt` sidecar alongside the original (the tier decision lives entirely in the runtime worker — no sandbox round-trip; the raw `AssistantFile` ref is threaded through the existing `RuntimeAttachmentRef.fileRef`/`objectKey` already carried on document jobs). **Sandbox** (`sandbox.service.ts`): `execute_document_code` materializes mounted sources + OCR sidecars under `/workspace/sources`, writes the program to a transient `/workspace/.document-code.py`, runs `python3` via the exec-pod bridge, and cleans up both the program and the sources dir in a `finally` so they are not collected as produced files; `inferMimeType` gains `.xlsx`/`.docx`. **Tool schema/catalog**: `create_data_document` + xlsx/docx documented (model-facing projection + tool-catalog guidance), CREATE-only (no revise/export for data docs). **Tests**: runtime adapter mode-B suite (xlsx happy path, self-repair, terminal double-failure, invalid-artifact, Tier-1 digital-PDF mounted with no OCR, Tier-2 scanned-PDF OCR sidecar); routing tests (`create_data_document` → data_document+sandbox, xlsx default, docx); enqueue `resolveExecutionShape` tests; sandbox `execute_document_code` test (mounts sources, writes OCR sidecar, runs `python3`, cleans transients). Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api`/`@persai/web`/`@persai/runtime`/`@persai/provider-gateway`/`@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · runtime tests PASS · sandbox 22/22 PASS · api tests PASS. **Deploy residual**: the additive enum migration `20260621000001_adr123_slice6_data_document` must run (it pauses on the `persai-dev-migrations` environment per CI policy).

- **ADR-123 sandbox exec image — preinstalled Python stack now reachable from login shells (root cause of "assistants see an empty Python"):** The model's `shell` tool runs commands through a login shell (`/bin/sh -lc`). On Debian a login shell sources `/etc/profile`, which hard-resets `PATH` to the distro default and drops `/opt/venv/bin` — so `python3`/`pip`/`weasyprint` resolved to the bare system interpreter (only `pip`/`setuptools`/`wheel`) instead of the Slice-4 venv stack (`pandas`/`numpy`/`weasyprint`/`openpyxl`/…). Verified in-cluster: `sh -c` kept `/opt/venv/bin` on PATH (stack visible) while `sh -lc` did not (stack hidden), and `/usr/bin/python3 -m pip list` matched exactly what the model reported. Fix (`apps/sandbox/exec-image/Dockerfile`): add `/etc/profile.d/10-venv.sh` (`export PATH="/opt/venv/bin:$PATH"`), which `/etc/profile` sources AFTER its PATH reset, so the venv is authoritative across login, non-login, and direct exec; the build self-check is extended with a login-shell `import weasyprint, pandas` so the guarantee fails loudly if it ever regresses. No image-stack change; ships in the next `sandbox-exec` image build. (Also folds in a prettier reflow of the Slice-1 push-fix strings in `exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`.)

- **ADR-123 Slice 5 landed (PDF cutover — pdfmonkey removed, WeasyPrint/sandbox renderer live):** Full switch of PDF document rendering from the external PDFMonkey SaaS API to in-sandbox WeasyPrint (already installed in the Slice 4 exec image). The chunked PDF generation pipeline is removed in full; truncation and timeout now retry single-shot. Enhanced print CSS is always applied (env flag removed). Sandbox-produced PDF files are downloaded from GCS, validated, and persisted as canonical `runtime_output` artifacts; the transient `sandbox_output` AssistantFile is soft-deleted via new `RuntimeAssistantFileRegistryService.deleteById()`. The Prisma enum value `pdfmonkey` is renamed to `sandbox` via migration SQL. Removed: `PdfMonkeyProviderClient`, pdfmonkey branch in provider-gateway document service, `documentProviderTemplateIds` from tool-credential input type, all pdfmonkey credential/template UI in web admin, pdfmonkey pricing entry, pdfmonkey display labels. Tests: `@persai/sandbox` gains a `render_html_to_pdf` unit test asserting `weasyprint` command + transient HTML cleanup. All five typechecks, full lint, format:check PASS. Unit test suites: `@persai/runtime` 41/41 PASS, `@persai/sandbox` 21/21 PASS, `@persai/api` PASS, `@persai/provider-gateway` PASS. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api`/`@persai/web`/`@persai/runtime`/`@persai/provider-gateway`/`@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · all unit test suites PASS.

## 2026-06-20

- **ADR-123 live shell fixes — exec RBAC verb + reliable workspace push (two root causes, both verified in-cluster):** Live testing showed every `shell` job failing after its exec pod was already Running (`violationCode: sandbox_failed`, `violationMessage: "[object Object]"`). Independent in-cluster reproduction (raw HTTPS exec probe + the actual `@kubernetes/client-node` from inside the control-plane pod) pinned two distinct causes. **(1) pods/exec RBAC verb (`infra/helm/templates/sandbox-serviceaccount.yaml`):** the client opens its exec stream over a WebSocket upgrade, which the API server issues as an HTTP **GET** and authorizes as verb `get` on `pods/exec`; the Role granted only `create` (the legacy SPDY/POST verb), so exec was rejected with `403 ... cannot get resource "pods/exec"` while plain pod create/get/delete (REST) worked. Granted `["get", "create"]`; applied live (`kubectl patch role`, matches git so selfHeal converges) and the raw probe then returned `101 Switching Protocols`. **(2) workspace push (`apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`):** `pushWorkspace` piped a live `tar -cf - -C ws .` child stdout straight into the exec WebSocket stdin and extracted with `tar -xf - -C /workspace`. The `.` archive member made the remote tar restore mode/utime on `/workspace` itself — the non-root (uid 1000) exec user cannot, so every push died with `tar: .: Cannot change mode/utime: Operation not permitted` (exit 2); separately, streaming a live child-process pipe as exec stdin raced the WebSocket EOF signal and intermittently truncated the archive or hung. Fix: archive top-level entries **by name** via new `createLocalTarball()` (never `.`; empty workspace skips push), **buffer** the whole archive, stream `Readable.from([buffer])` (a fully materialized readable delivers reliably), and extract with `tar --no-same-owner -xf - -C /workspace` so extraction never touches `/workspace` metadata. **(3) error visibility:** the three exec WebSocket paths passed raw rejections (a non-Error `ErrorEvent`) straight through, so `String(error)` collapsed the real API-server message to `"[object Object]"`; new `describeUnknownError()` extracts the real text. Verified end to end in persai-dev: push → exec (`pandas`/`numpy`/`openpyxl` import OK) → pull round-trip (a file created in the pod returns to the control plane). Gate: `@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · sandbox tests 19/19 PASS (new regression test asserts the push command uses `--no-same-owner` and never includes a `.` member) · helm lint PASS · format:check PASS. RBAC change applies on sync; the bridge change ships in the next `sandbox` image build.

- **ADR-123 foundation (Slices 1–4) deployed and live-healthy on persai-dev + two post-deploy fixes:** The staged validation deploy is green — ArgoCD `persai-dev` is `Synced`/`Healthy` on the foundation, with the control-plane `sandbox` running the hardened ADR-123 manifest on image `2717fcf2` (both replicas `2/2`, `/ready` passing) and the `sandbox-egress-proxy` (Squid) `1/1` stable. Two gaps surfaced only at live rollout and were fixed cleanly: **(1) cluster-ops — missing `roles/cloudsql.client` on `sandbox-cp`:** the sandbox Deployment now runs under `sandbox-sa` → `sandbox-cp` (not `api-sa`), and its cloud-sql-proxy sidecar was denied (`403 missing permission cloudsql.instances.get`), so the DB was unreachable and `/ready` returned 503. Granted `roles/cloudsql.client` to `sandbox-cp` at project level; documented as a REQUIRED step in `infra/dev/gke/RUNBOOK.md` (§2b). **(2) egress-proxy non-root (`infra/helm/templates/sandbox-egress-proxy.yaml`):** after the dstdomain + privilege-drop fixes, Squid still crash-looped with `FATAL: Cannot open '/dev/stdout' for writing` — starting as root and dropping to `proxy` left `/dev/stdout` (owned by PID 1) unwritable by the dropped worker. Now the container runs directly as the image's unprivileged `proxy` user (`runAsUser/Group: 13`, `fsGroup: 13`, `runAsNonRoot: true`): PID 1 is `proxy` so `/dev/stdout` is writable for access logging, no root→proxy switch is needed (caps `drop: [ALL]`, SETUID/SETGID removed), and emptyDir volumes are group-writable. The benign `ICMP pinger ... Operation not permitted` log line is expected (no `NET_RAW`) and does not affect L7 proxying. **ArgoCD recovery note:** the auto-sync had wedged in a phantom `operationState.phase=Running` after a PreSync `api-migrate` hook Job was caught between its `ttlSecondsAfterFinished` deletion and the `argocd.argoproj.io/hook-finalizer`; cleared by removing the stale Job finalizer and the stuck `status.operationState`, after which a fresh sync ran the hook clean and applied all manifests.

- **ADR-123 Slice 4 landed (exec image — Python + Node + doc/data stack + Chromium + ripgrep/fd):** Replaced the placeholder `busybox:1.36` exec image with the real in-sandbox toolchain (ADR-123 D5). New standalone image registered as a distinct CI deploy service (`sandbox-exec`) — separate from the control-plane `sandbox` service. **Exec image** (`apps/sandbox/exec-image/Dockerfile` + `requirements.txt`): base `debian:bookworm-slim`; installs bash, coreutils, tar, ca-certificates, curl; Python 3 (Debian 3.11) in an isolated venv at `/opt/venv` with `pandas 3.0.3`, `numpy 2.4.6`, `matplotlib 3.11.0`, `openpyxl 3.1.5`, `python-docx 1.2.0`, `weasyprint 69.0`, `pdfplumber 0.11.10`, `Pillow 12.2.0`; Node.js 22 LTS (NodeSource); `ripgrep` (`rg`) + `fd-find` (symlinked to `fd`); headless `chromium`; fonts `fonts-dejavu`, `fonts-liberation`, `fonts-noto`, `fonts-noto-cjk` (Cyrillic/CJK); fontconfig; `fc-cache` baked in. Non-root user `sandbox` uid=1000/gid=1000. `ENV HOME=/workspace` (writable emptyDir at runtime) so the model's files and runtime `pip install --user` packages persist across the session; regenerable tool caches are redirected to the ephemeral `/tmp` emptyDir via `XDG_CACHE_HOME=/tmp/.cache` and `MPLCONFIGDIR=/tmp/.matplotlib` so they never pollute the persisted `/workspace` snapshot. Build-time self-checks verify every tool and Python import — a broken build fails loudly. **readOnlyRootFilesystem compliance**: all tools installed in immutable image layers; only `/workspace` (emptyDir, session-scoped) and `/tmp` (emptyDir, raised to 256Mi in `exec-pod-bridge.service.ts` to host the toolchain's `/tmp` caches + Chromium profile) writable at runtime. **Chromium note for Slice 5**: must run with `--no-sandbox --headless=new --user-data-dir=/tmp/chromium-profile` (gVisor is the isolation boundary; `--user-data-dir=/tmp` keeps profile in writable /tmp). **CI integration** (`scripts/ci/detect-affected.mjs`): `sandbox-exec` added to `APP_METADATA` (standalone; no pnpm workspace); `classifyFile` routes `apps/sandbox/exec-image/**` changes to `sandbox-exec` deploy (not the control-plane `sandbox`); `NON_WORKSPACE_DEPLOY_SERVICES` includes `sandbox-exec` for `workflow_dispatch` coverage. 3 new tests in `detect-affected.test.mjs` (exec-image → sandbox-exec only; requirements.txt → sandbox-exec only; src change → sandbox not sandbox-exec). **SHA pinning** (`scripts/ci/pin-dev-image-tags.mjs`): `"sandbox-exec": "sandboxExec"` added to `serviceToSection`; pin script validated dry-run. **Helm** (`infra/helm/values-dev.yaml` + `sandbox-deployment.yaml`): new `sandboxExec.image` block (`name: sandbox-exec`, `tag: dev-main`); `SANDBOX_EXEC_IMAGE` removed from `sandbox.env` and instead computed explicitly in the deployment template from `sandboxExec.image.{registryHost,projectId,repository,name,tag}` (falls back to `global.images.tag` if `sandboxExec.image.tag` is unset); rendered value: `europe-west1-docker.pkg.dev/…/persai/sandbox-exec:dev-main`. **sandbox-config.ts**: default `busybox:1.36` retained for local dev (no cluster; value satisfies Zod non-empty validation but is not used without a live k8s API). `apps/runtime` untouched. Local docker build not attempted (Docker Desktop not running); image build is CI/GAR-validated. **Tests**: sandbox 18/18 PASS (no change — config untouched); detect-affected 7/7 PASS (4 pre-existing + 3 new). Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/web` typecheck PASS · `@persai/runtime` typecheck PASS · `@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · sandbox tests 18/18 PASS · helm lint PASS · helm template PASS · detect-affected 7/7 PASS · pin script dry-run PASS.

- **ADR-123 Slice 3 landed (per-session pod reuse, idle-TTL reaper, GCS workspace snapshot):** Session-lived sandbox execution: pods are now reused across jobs within a session instead of created/destroyed per job. Pod name for session jobs is derived deterministically from `runtimeSessionId` via SHA-256 — format `ses-<sha256[0..31]>` (stable, k8s-safe, 36 chars ≤ 63 limit). Sessionless jobs (null `runtimeSessionId`) retain the Slice 1 ephemeral create/delete behavior unchanged. **Session lifecycle** (`apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`): `runInPod` splits into `runInSessionPod` (reuse path) and `runInEphemeralPod` (ephemeral path). `ensureSessionPodRunning` checks k8s state directly — reuses if Running, creates if absent, recreates if terminal. `lastActivityAt` is updated at the start and end of each session job to protect against reaper eviction during execution. **Idle-TTL reaper**: `OnModuleInit` starts a `setInterval` reaper; `runReaperTick()` iterates the in-memory `sessionPods` map and calls `deletePod` for entries idle longer than `SANDBOX_EXEC_SESSION_IDLE_TTL_MS` (default 30 min). Reaper sweep interval: `SANDBOX_EXEC_REAPER_INTERVAL_MS` (default 2 min). Both configurable via `sandbox-config.ts` and `values-dev.yaml`. **Serialization**: the existing `assistantId+workspaceId` Postgres lease mutex already serializes all jobs for a session — no additional locking needed. **GCS workspace snapshot** (`apps/sandbox/src/sandbox.service.ts`): after each successful session job, the entire workspace directory is tar'd and saved to GCS as `{prefix}/assistants/{assistantId}/sandbox-sessions/{runtimeSessionId}/workspace.tar` (new `buildSessionSnapshotKey` in `SandboxObjectStorageService`). On pod recreate (state token mismatch during `ensureWorkspaceSessionHydrated`): after declared `AssistantFile` records are restored, `restoreSessionSnapshotOverlay` extracts the snapshot into a staging dir and copies only files absent from the workspace (copy-if-absent via `fs.cp({ force: false })`) to add back ephemeral files without overwriting declared content. This avoids the GNU-vs-BSD tar divergence (`--keep-old-files` errors on pre-existing files under GNU tar; `--skip-old-files` is missing on BSD tar). Missing snapshot (first session) is handled gracefully with a `warn` log. All tar operations are soft-fail (log warn + continue) for resilience. **Invariants preserved**: exec pods still have ZERO secrets, `automountServiceAccountToken: false`, `runtimeClassName: gvisor`, hardened securityContext, proxy-only egress. GCS creds remain control-plane-only. **Warm pool DEFERRED**: cold-start (~2–4s gVisor) is acceptable at current scale; ADR-123 Slice 3 notes it as a future optimization. **Config**: `SANDBOX_EXEC_SESSION_IDLE_TTL_MS` (default 1800000 ms), `SANDBOX_EXEC_REAPER_INTERVAL_MS` (default 120000 ms). `apps/runtime` untouched. **Tests** (18/18 pass): session pod name stable from session ID; sessionless falls back to ephemeral with delete; second session job reuses pod (no recreate, no delete); reaper evicts idle pods and updates map; session snapshot save uses correct assistant+session GCS key; no-op restore on missing snapshot; round-trip save→restore adds ephemeral files without overwriting declared files. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/web` typecheck PASS · `@persai/runtime` typecheck PASS · `@persai/sandbox` typecheck PASS · sandbox tests 18/18 PASS · helm lint PASS · helm template PASS.

- **ADR-123 Slice 2 landed (egress proxy + deny-all exec pod network boundary):** Kernel-level network isolation for gVisor exec pods: deny-all egress NetworkPolicy + trusted Squid proxy with domain allowlist. **NetworkPolicy** (`infra/helm/templates/networkpolicies.yaml`): `sandbox-exec-deny-egress` selects exec pods (`app.kubernetes.io/component: sandbox-exec`), `policyTypes: [Egress]`, default-deny, allowing only kube-dns (UDP+TCP port 53, namespaceSelector `kube-system`) and the proxy pod (TCP 3128) when `egressProxy.enabled`. `sandbox-egress-proxy-isolation` for the proxy pod: ingress only from exec pods on 3128; egress to DNS + internet on TCP 80/443 (L7 enforcement delegated to Squid). **Egress proxy** (`infra/helm/templates/sandbox-egress-proxy.yaml`): Squid Deployment + Service + ConfigMap; port 3128; allowlist enforced via `acl allowed_domains dstdomain` + `http_access deny all`; hardened securityContext (`allowPrivilegeEscalation: false`, `drop ALL caps`, `seccomp RuntimeDefault`); cache disabled; writable emptyDirs for `/var/spool/squid`, `/var/log/squid`, `/run`; no on-disk state. **Allowed domains** (`values-dev.yaml`): `pypi.org` + `.pypi.org` + `files.pythonhosted.org` + `.files.pythonhosted.org` (pip install), `registry.npmjs.org` + `.registry.npmjs.org` (npm install) — nothing else. **Config** (`packages/config/src/sandbox-config.ts`): `SANDBOX_EXEC_EGRESS_PROXY_URL` (default `""`) and `SANDBOX_EXEC_NO_PROXY` (default `""`). **Bridge** (`apps/sandbox/src/exec-pod-bridge.service.ts`): `createExecPod` now calls `buildProxyEnv()` — when proxy URL is non-empty, injects `HTTP_PROXY`, `HTTPS_PROXY`, `http_proxy`, `https_proxy` (all set to the proxy URL), plus `NO_PROXY`/`no_proxy` when configured; when proxy URL is empty, `env: []` (no secrets ever injected, secret boundary intact). **values-dev.yaml**: `SANDBOX_EXEC_EGRESS_PROXY_URL: "http://sandbox-egress-proxy.persai-dev.svc.cluster.local:3128"`, `SANDBOX_EXEC_NO_PROXY` set with loopback + RFC1918 + in-cluster bypass list; `sandbox.egressProxy` block with image, port, allowedDomains, resources. **Tests**: 2 new tests in `exec-pod-bridge.service.test.ts` — proxy env vars injected when URL set (6 vars asserted), none when URL empty; `sandbox-metrics.service.test.ts` config fixture updated. `apps/runtime` untouched. - **Follow-up — multi-step working notes (`workingNotes: string[]` replaces single `workingPreamble`/`preambleText`; no new ADR):** The single pre-first-tool "working preamble" string was replaced end to end by an ordered array of per-step notes — the text the model writes BEFORE each tool call across every tool-loop iteration (empty array = no notes). **Runtime** (`turn-execution.service.ts`): notes are now captured on EVERY `tool_calls` event (was: once, only `iteration === 0`) from that iteration's own `event.result.text` (per-iteration, NOT the cumulative `assembledText`, which would re-include earlier steps). New pure exported `assembleWorkingNotesAndAnswer({ toolStepTexts, finalAnswerText, fullAssistantText })` returns `{ workingNotes, answerText, assistantText }`; the prior `splitPreambleAndAnswer` was removed. **Duplication trap (the bug from the prior cut):** `providerResult.text` on the final `completed` is the CUMULATIVE corrected text (all notes + answer) — so `answerText` is taken from the final iteration's own text (`correctedFinalAnswerText`), never the cumulative text, and `assistantText` stays the verbatim cumulative corrected text. Invariants (locked in tests): `workingNotes = [note0, note1, …]` each exactly once (only its iteration's pre-tool text); `answerText` = final answer only, no notes; `assistantText` = each note exactly once then the answer (no dupes); no-tools turn → `workingNotes=[]`, `answerText===assistantText`; empty final answer after tools → `answerText=""`; whitespace-only note dropped. **Contract:** `RuntimeTurnResult.preambleText` → `workingNotes: string[]` (`runtime-contract`); `AssistantWebChatMessageState.workingPreamble` → `workingNotes` (array of strings) in `openapi.yaml`, contracts regenerated. **API:** done chunk carries `workingNotes` (`web-runtime-stream-client.service.ts`, `assistant-runtime.facade.ts`); `persist-assistant-message.ts` takes `workingNotes?: string[]` and writes `metadata.workingNotes` only when non-empty; `web-chat-message-state.mapper.ts` `extractWorkingPreambleFromMetadata` → `extractWorkingNotesFromMetadata` (`string[]`); `web-chat.types.ts` updated. **Symptom-1 fix:** the live `completed` transport in `stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts` (variable renamed `runtimeWorkingPreamble` → `runtimeWorkingNotes`) now includes `workingNotes` on the hand-built `assistantMessage`, so the "Выполнено" block appears without reopening the chat. **UI:** `assistant-api-client.ts`, `use-chat.ts` (`ChatMessage`, `toCommittedChatMessage`, both `onCompleted` handlers), and `chat-message.tsx` (`WorkingTextBlocks` now reads `message.workingNotes` directly — no `\n\n` split). **Backfill:** `backfill-working-preamble.ts` → idempotent `backfill-working-notes.ts` (skip rows already in `workingNotes` form; `metadata.workingPreamble` string → `[workingPreamble]`; legacy `:::working` content markers → parsed `workingNotes` + cleaned content). **Tests:** new `assemble-working-notes-and-answer.test.ts` (registered in both run-suites) + new `backfill-working-notes.test.ts`; multi-step capture asserted in `turn-execution.service.test.ts` (two `tool_calls` → `workingNotes=["First plan.","Second plan."]`, `answerText="Final answer."`, `assistantText` each note once then answer — the assertion fails on the naive cumulative-as-answer impl, verified by temporary revert, and passes after the fix); web/api suites migrated off the old field name. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api`/`@persai/web`/`@persai/runtime`/`@persai/runtime-contract` typecheck PASS · `stream-web-chat-turn.service.test.ts` 15/15 · `backfill-working-notes.test.ts` 9/9 · runtime assemble + turn-execution tests PASS · web `chat-message`/`use-chat`/`chat-message-streaming` 132/132. No `workingPreamble`/`preambleText` remain outside the backfill's legacy-read paths and historical CHANGELOG/handoff entries.

- **ADR-122 Slice 3 landed (truncation guard — model no longer continues a cut-off answer):** Orthogonal `truncated?: boolean` signal propagated end-to-end. Provider clients: Anthropic sets `truncated: response.stop_reason === "max_tokens"` (non-stream) / `latestStopReason === "max_tokens"` (stream); OpenAI adds `isMaxOutputTokensTruncation()` checking `response.status === "incomplete" && incomplete_details.reason === "max_output_tokens"` and promotes the `response.incomplete` event from a failed event to a completed+truncated event when the reason is `max_output_tokens`. `RuntimeTurnResult.truncated` propagates from the final provider result in `buildTurnResult`. API: `AssistantRuntimeWebChatTurnStreamChunk.truncated?: boolean` added; `done` chunk forwards `truncated: true` when present; `persist-assistant-message.ts` gains `truncatedStatus?: "truncated"` (orthogonal to existing `partialStatus?: "partial"`); `stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts` persists `metadata.status = "truncated"` when the turn completed normally but was cut short. Hydration guard: `withTruncationMarker()` in `TurnContextHydrationService` appends `"\n\n[Note: the previous answer was interrupted before completion.]"` to any prior assistant message whose `metadata.status` is `"partial"` (abort) or `"truncated"` (max_tokens); applied in both the summarized-messages loop and the canonical web hydration loop; idempotent (marker checked before appending, stored content never contains it). Tests: Anthropic client max_tokens non-stream + stream cases; hydration marker (partial, truncated, clean, idempotency); `buildTurnResult` propagation. Gate: format:check PASS · `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/runtime` typecheck PASS · `@persai/provider-gateway` typecheck PASS · `@persai/web` typecheck PASS · all test suites PASS.

- **ADR-122 Slice 2 corrective pass (PROD-correct for BOTH providers; turn-0 thinking gap fixed):** Resolver formula corrected to reserve thinking inside the output ceiling: constants are now `OUTPUT_BUDGET_MAX = 128_000` (cap on FINAL answer+thinking), `OUTPUT_BUDGET_FALLBACK = 8_192` (base for null `maxOutputTokens`, safe on every mainstream model), `OUTPUT_BUDGET_FLOOR = 1_024`, `CONTEXT_SAFETY_RESERVE = 4_096` (`OUTPUT_BUDGET_SANITY_CAP` removed). Formula: `totalCeiling = min(maxOutputTokens ?? FALLBACK, MAX)`; `totalRoom = min(totalCeiling, contextWindow - input - reserve)`; `answer = totalRoom - thinkingBudget`; clamp `[FLOOR, MAX]` — so gateway `max_tokens = answer + thinkingBudget = totalRoom ≤ model ceiling`, eliminating the opus 128k+thinking 32768 overflow 400. OpenAI families seeded in `MODEL_CAPABILITY_DEFAULTS` (gpt-5.x = 400k/128k; gpt-4o(-mini) = 128k/16_384) — fixes the OpenAI 400 (it sends `max_output_tokens` verbatim, no clamp); unlisted OpenAI keys → fallback. Family defaults now fold in at READ (`parseRuntimeProviderModelProfiles`) AND WRITE (`normalizeModelProfiles`) normalization, not just synthesis, so PROD rows persisted with the brand-new null fields resolve to the published ceiling without a manual save (explicit admin value always wins; unknown model stays null; supersedes the earlier known-model "null strictly round-trips" note). Turn-0 extended thinking enabled — `prepareTurnExecution` passes the route thinking budget to both `buildProviderRequest` and the resolver (fixes ADR-121 turn-0 gap; safe because the gateway stream timeout is idle-based and watchdogs disabled). `PROVIDER_GATEWAY_STREAM_TIMEOUT_MS = 90_000` confirmed idle (resets on every stream event incl. thinking deltas). Gate: format:check PASS · resolver unit test PASS · runTurnExecutionServiceTest PASS · runAnthropicProviderClientTest PASS · api normalization + read-fold-in tests PASS · `@persai/api`/`@persai/web`/`@persai/runtime`/`@persai/provider-gateway` typecheck PASS.

- **ADR-122 Slice 2 landed (unified output-budget resolver, main-chat-turn truncation fix):** `resolveModelOutputBudget(capability, ctx)` introduced as the single pure resolver in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/model-output-budget.ts`. (The initial cut used an `OUTPUT_BUDGET_SANITY_CAP = 200_000` base/clamp and a context-only thinking subtraction; both were **superseded by the corrective-pass entry above** — final constants are `OUTPUT_BUDGET_MAX = 128_000` / `OUTPUT_BUDGET_FALLBACK = 8_192` with thinking reserved inside the ceiling. See that entry for the authoritative formula.) Wired into `prepareTurnExecution` (main turn — was the only path NOT setting `maxOutputTokens`) and `refreshProviderRequestMessages` via the new `resolveSlotCapability` helper and char-based `estimateProviderRequestInputTokens`. Tool-loop continuation inherits via spread. `runtime-document-provider-adapter.service.ts` `resolveMaxOutputTokens` refactored to delegate to the resolver (dead `DEFENSIVE_OUTPUT_TOKEN_CAP` retired). `anthropic-provider.client.ts` four `?? 1_024` literals replaced with `PROVIDER_FALLBACK_MAX_OUTPUT_TOKENS = 4_096`; thinking math (`max_tokens = answer + thinking`) preserved exactly. Bounded callers (auto-extract, router, compaction, media-job, background-task) confirmed to set their own explicit budgets — untouched. Tests: 9-case resolver unit test, `runTurnExecutionServiceTest` (with new maxOutputTokens regression guard), `runAnthropicProviderClientTest` (thinking semantics confirmed). Gate: `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/runtime` typecheck PASS · `@persai/provider-gateway` typecheck PASS · all tests PASS.

- **ADR-122 Slice 1 landed (maxOutputTokens + contextWindow as first-class model capability fields):** `maxOutputTokens: number | null` and `contextWindow: number | null` added as first-class admin-managed fields on `RuntimeProviderModelProfileBase`. `normalizeModelProfiles()` validates both via a new `normalizeOptionalPositiveInteger()` helper (null allowed; bounds: max 1_000_000 / 2_000_000). Routing slot type gains both fields; `resolve-runtime-provider-routing.service.ts` enriches every slot via `lookupModelCapabilities()` so Slice 2 can read the values from the slot directly. `MODEL_CAPABILITY_DEFAULTS` defined with authoritative Anthropic values (7 models, all 200k context window at non-premium tier; OpenAI left null). Seeding applied only at synthesis/legacy-row normalization — admin-set explicit values and explicit nulls on real catalog rows are untouched (null round-trips as null). Admin runtime UI gains a `NullableIntegerField` component and two new inputs per model row ("Max output tokens", "Context window"). `RuntimeProviderModelProfileCommonState` in `openapi.yaml` gains both nullable integer fields; contracts regenerated. - **Docs-only — formal closure of ADR-120 and ADR-121 (no code/deploy):** Reconciled ADR status with shipped reality. ADR-120 header was stale (it still listed the two tracked residuals — HNSW index + legacy JSONB column drop — as "pending" while its own Closure II section recorded them resolved); flipped status `closure-mode` → **Closed** and rewrote the blockquote to state both residuals are resolved. ADR-121 was still framed "Open program ADR / Accepted" despite all five slices being landed, deployed, and live-validated; flipped to **Closed** and appended a `## Closure (2026-06-20)` section (per-slice summary + the live-found `slow_avg` watchdog fix). `AGENTS.md` startup-reading closed-archive list now includes ADR-120 and ADR-121 so neither is treated as active backlog. No source, schema, or runtime change.

- **Follow-up fix — runtime preamble/answer split regression (same slice as the tool-loop final-answer fix below):** The first cut of the preamble split in `apps/runtime/src/modules/turns/turn-execution.service.ts` (`buildTurnResult`) was wrong: it set `answerText = providerResult.text` (the FULL corrected `preamble + answer` text) and `assistantText = preamble + "\n\n" + answerText`, so for a tool-loop turn with preamble `P` and answer `A` it produced `answerText = "P A"` (preamble duplicated into the answer → web) and `assistantText = "P\n\nP A"` (doubled preamble → Telegram). It went undetected because the API golden tests mock the runtime stream and inject `finalAnswer`/`workingPreamble` directly into the `done` chunk, never exercising the runtime split. **Fix:** extracted a pure, exported, unit-tested `splitPreambleAndAnswer(fullText, preambleText)` — `assistantText` is now `providerResult.text` verbatim (the canonical full corrected text, single preamble, never reconstructed) and `answerText` is the full text with the captured preamble stripped (verbatim-prefix → left-trimmed retry → safe full-text fallback if the preamble is not a prefix, so content is never silently dropped). `buildTurnResult` now delegates to it. Invariants: tool-loop → `preambleText=P`, `answerText=A`, `assistantText=full`; no-tools → `preambleText=null`, `answerText=assistantText=full`; empty answer after tools → `answerText=""`, `assistantText=P`; whitespace-only preamble → `null`. **Tests:** new runtime unit suite `apps/runtime/test/split-preamble-and-answer.test.ts` (registered in both `run-suite.ts` and `run-suite-isolated.ts`), plus `preambleText`/`answerText` assertions added to the streaming tool-loop + no-tools cases in `turn-execution.service.test.ts` (the integration assertions fail on the buggy logic and pass after the fix — verified by temporarily reverting). Contract (`preambleText`/`answerText`/`finalAnswer`/`workingPreamble`), backfill, and UI are unchanged. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/web` typecheck PASS · `@persai/runtime` typecheck PASS · `stream-web-chat-turn.service.test.ts` 21/21 PASS · `backfill-working-preamble.test.ts` PASS · new runtime split test PASS · full `runTurnExecutionServiceTest` PASS.

- **Production bug fix — tool-loop final answer loss (ADR-120 era; no new ADR needed):** Fixed a two-part defect that caused tool-loop chat turns to persist only the pre-tool "working" preamble while discarding the final answer. Root cause: (1) the API `completed` event consumer gated acceptance of `event.result.assistantText` on `assistantText.startsWith(accumulated)` — runtime sanitization and merge separators broke that prefix check so the final text was silently dropped; (2) the API persistence layer wrapped pre-tool text in synthetic `:::working\n...\n:::` markers and stored that as `content` rather than the real final answer. Fix: (A) `RuntimeTurnResult` extended with `preambleText` + `answerText` split; (B) `startsWith` gate removed from `case "completed"` in the API SSE consumer; `finalAnswer` / `workingPreamble` forwarded on the `done` chunk; (C) entire `:::working` pipeline removed from `stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts`; content is now `answerText`, preamble is `metadata.workingPreamble`; aborted/stalled turns persist `metadata.status = "partial"`; (D) one-shot idempotent backfill script `apps/api/prisma/backfill-working-preamble.ts` converts legacy rows; (E) frontend `WorkingTextBlocks` now sources blocks from `message.workingPreamble` instead of parsing `:::working` markers from `content`; all legacy working-block parsing functions removed from `chat-message-streaming.ts` and `use-chat.ts`; (F) `AssistantWebChatMessageState` gains `workingPreamble?: string | null` in openapi.yaml + regenerated contracts. Gate: lint PASS · format:check PASS · `@persai/api` typecheck PASS · `@persai/web` typecheck PASS · `stream-web-chat-turn.service.test.ts` 15/15 PASS · `backfill-working-preamble.test.ts` 6/6 PASS · web tests 69 files / all PASS.

- **ADR-120 landed (RAG/Knowledge unification + memory JIT — pull-first retrieval, single vector store, honest relevance):** program `docs/ADR/120-rag-knowledge-unification-and-memory-jit.md` implemented across seven bounded slices (`d007025b` ADR open · `0e36d959` S1 · `7fd6eeb1` S2 · `1ae3c201` S3 · `fce1e698` S4 · `89046014` S5 · `951580bd` S6 · this closure commit S7). Both adjacent "push large, low-relevance context every turn" subsystems (durable memory + RAG) were reworked onto one principle: **the model pulls what it needs; the server stops pushing "just in case."**
  - **Memory JIT (S1–S2):** the always-on pushed contextual short-memory block was retired end to end — `<persai_memory>` / `durable_memory_contextual` volatile entries are no longer spliced into the recency zone, eliminating cross-chat memory bleeding by construction; `HydrateMemoryForTurnService` now returns the durable `core` block only (stable AOT prefix, global by design). Cross-chat / old-fact recall became **pull-only** via the `knowledge_search` `memory` source. Open loops are scoped to the **current chat + open-only** (`chatId = current` AND `resolvedAt IS NULL`) for both the open-loop refs developer block and the close-by-similarity path; additive composite index migration `20260619230000_adr120_memory_chat_scope_index`.
  - **RAG engine (S3):** user-knowledge + product/global document reads switched from the legacy "first-N rows by table order + in-process cosine" candidate selection to the unified `KnowledgeVectorChunk` pgvector **ANN** query (`ORDER BY embedding_vector <=> query::vector`, the path skills already used) — true nearest-neighbour candidate selection fixes relevance at the root. The dual-persist **legacy JSONB chunk write is retained this release** as rollback safety (see follow-ups). An idempotent parity backfill (`backfill-knowledge-vector-store`) reconciles the vector store from existing source chunks.
  - **RAG precision (S4):** the relevance floor (`passesRelevanceFloor`, score + top-K margin) is now applied to **all** sources including documents/files (previously only memory/chat); the LLM rerank no longer fail-opens into widened lexical order — when the helper is unavailable the engine falls back to ANN-score order **without widening, floor still applied**; the `MIN_CONTEXT_ITEMS = 4` floor was removed so retrieval may return **empty** (no-answer beats wrong-answer).
  - **Pull-first unified (S5):** the entire always-on server push subsystem was removed — the orchestrate retrieval service + controller + tests, the `POST /api/v1/internal/runtime/knowledge/orchestrate` internal endpoint, the runtime client method, the flat `# Retrieved Knowledge Context` developer block, and the `RuntimeRetrievedKnowledgeContext*` contract types. The ADR-119 `<persai_retrieved_knowledge>` push contract is **superseded by pull** (ADR-120 D6): retrieved knowledge flows back exclusively as `knowledge_search` / `knowledge_fetch` tool results. The skill KB became a gated `knowledge_search`/`knowledge_fetch` source; project mode no longer force-sets `useUserKnowledge` and instead guarantees the retrieval tools are projected (pull-dispatch contract — "locate with search, read with fetch; one excerpt is not sufficiency").
  - **Config (S6):** snippet-first is the new default — admin `smartSearchEnabled` ceiling default flipped `true → false` (default-only, no migration); the atomic `skill_knowledge_card` exception returns its FULL card text inline even when smart search is snippet-only. The admin Plans UI gained a `lean` / `balanced` / `rich` retrieval preset dropdown (UI fill-helper only — fills all 16 raw draft fields; no persisted `retrievalPolicy.preset`, no contract change) with the 16 raw knobs moved under an "Advanced retrieval knobs" disclosure.
  - **Closure (S7):** docs finalized (this entry + `SESSION-HANDOFF`, ADR status → Accepted/closure-mode, API-BOUNDARY/DATA-MODEL pull-first corrections) and the ADR-120 golden invariant locked in both prompt-snapshot tests (`apps/runtime/test/adr119-golden-prompt-snapshot.test.ts` + `apps/api/test/adr119-golden-prompt-snapshot.test.ts`): explicit negative assertions that no `<persai_memory>` push, no `# Retrieved Knowledge Context` block, and no pushed `<persai_retrieved_knowledge>` block appear in the assembled context, plus a positive check that `knowledge_search` / `knowledge_fetch` are the pull retrieval path. Golden tests green (api + runtime).
  - **Tracked follow-ups (residuals, NOT new scope, do NOT reopen the program):** (1) **HNSW ANN index** on `knowledge_vector_chunks.embedding_vector` is **deferred** — the `embedding_vector` column is dimensionless; pin `vector(N)` and build the `hnsw` (`vector_cosine_ops`) index once the live embedding model/dimension is confirmed. Correct ANN already ships via sequential scan. (2) **Legacy JSONB chunk columns** are **kept this release** as rollback safety; drop them in a follow-up migration after PROD confirms vector reads healthy and the post-deploy backfill has run.
  - **Post-deploy step:** run the parity backfill (`corepack pnpm --filter @persai/api run backfill:knowledge-vector-store`) in PROD after deploy, then confirm vector-store reads are healthy before scheduling the two follow-ups.
- **ADR-120 Closure II — vector store hardening + legacy embedding column retirement:** resolved the two ADR-120 tracked follow-ups now that the parity backfill is complete and PROD `knowledge_vector_chunks` is uniform `vector(3072)` (982 rows, all text-embedding-3-large; 2 stale sources reindexed to 3072). **(1) HNSW ANN index added** — migration `20260620120000_adr120_drop_legacy_chunk_jsonb_and_hnsw` creates `knowledge_vector_chunks_embedding_hnsw_idx` on a `halfvec(3072)` expression (`halfvec_cosine_ops`), since pgvector 0.8.1 caps the bare `vector` type at 2000 dims for HNSW; `KnowledgeVectorIndex.searchNearest` now orders by `embedding_vector::halfvec(3072) <=> query::halfvec(3072)` so the planner uses the index, and re-scores the returned top-K at full `vector` precision (the `1 - (… <=> …::vector)` score line is unchanged). The stored column type stays `vector(3072)`. **(2) Legacy JSONB embedding columns dropped** — the same migration drops `embedding_vector` + `embedding_generated_at` from `assistant_knowledge_source_chunks`, `global_knowledge_source_chunks`, and `product_knowledge_text_entry_chunks` (NON-reversible data loss; the unified store is now authoritative). These three tables remain the canonical TEXT store (`content`/`locator`/`embedding_model_key` retained). The indexing worker (`persistLegacyChunkRows`) stops dual-writing the JSONB embeddings; vectors continue to flow to `KnowledgeVectorChunk` via `replaceSourceChunks`. The completed one-time backfill runner/service (`BackfillKnowledgeVectorStoreService`, its script, test, module registration, and the `backfill:knowledge-vector-store` npm script) were removed. Full retirement of the legacy `*_chunks` tables themselves remains a separate future program.

## 2026-06-19

- **Disabled stale slow-mo cadence watchdog (`slow_avg`) for web chat streams (live-found post-ADR-121 fix):** `resolveWebStreamCadenceWatchdogOptions` in `stream-web-chat-turn.service.ts` now returns `slowAvgEnabled: false` for normal/smart chat modes (it was already `false` for `project`, and `silentEnabled` is `false` everywhere) — so the cadence watchdog never reports a stall. Root cause found during live validation on `persai.dev`: with ADR-121 routing now reliably selecting the reasoning-tier model (`claude-opus-4-8`) for deep-level turns, that model streams visible text below the per-token `slow_avg` threshold (avg inter-delta gap > 200ms over 20 samples), which tripped `slow_avg`, aborted the runtime fetch mid-answer, and produced a truncated reply with no clean `stream-end`. Real mid-stream hangs remain guarded by the provider/runtime stream timeout (`PERSAI_RUNTIME_STREAM_TIMEOUT_MS`); the watchdog scaffolding, telemetry (`web_stream_stall_*`), and stall-retry path are retained and remain config-reenableable. Test `stream-web-chat-turn.service.test.ts` updated to assert both signals disabled in all chat modes.
